;;; !(import! &self Unify.metta)
;;; Enumerate all programs up to a given depth that are consistent with
;;; the query, using the given axiom non-deterministic functions and rules.
;;;
;;; The arguments are:
;;;
;;; $query: an Atom under the form (: TERM TYPE).  The atom may contain
;;;         free variables within TERM and TYPE to form various sort of
;;;         queries, such as:
;;;         1. Backward chaining: (: $term (Inheritance $x Mammal))
;;;         2. Forward chaining: (: ($rule $premise AXIOM) $type)
;;;         3. Mixed chaining: (: ($rule $premise AXIOM) (Inheritance $x Mammal))
;;;         4. Type checking: (: TERM TYPE)
;;;         5. Type inference: (: TERM $type)
;;;
;;; $kb: a nullary function to axiom, to non-deterministically pick up
;;;      an axiom.  An axiom is an Atom of the form (: TERM TYPE).
;;;
;;; $rb: a nullary function to rule, to non-deterministically pick up a
;;;      rule.  A rule is a function mapping premises to conclusion,
;;;      where premises and conclusion have the form (: TERM TYPE).
;;;
;;; $depth: a Nat representing the maximum depth of the generated
;;;         programs.
;;;
;;; TODO: recurse over curried rules instead of duplicating code over
;;; tuples.
;;; Collection of functions operating on numbers

;;; Define max
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[:,max,[->,'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a)]])
(: max 
  (-> $a $a $a))


  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[=,[max,'$VAR'(x),'$VAR'(y)],[if,[>,'$VAR'(x),'$VAR'(y)],'$VAR'(x),'$VAR'(y)]])
(= 
  (max $x $y) 
  (if 
    (> $x $y) $x $y))


;;; Define min
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[:,min,[->,'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a)]])
(: min 
  (-> $a $a $a))


  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[=,[min,'$VAR'(x),'$VAR'(y)],[if,[<,'$VAR'(x),'$VAR'(y)],'$VAR'(x),'$VAR'(y)]])
(= 
  (min $x $y) 
  (if 
    (< $x $y) $x $y))


;;; Clamp a number to be within a certain range
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[:,clamp,[->,'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a)]])
(: clamp 
  (-> $a $a $a $a))


  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[=,[clamp,'$VAR'(x),'$VAR'(l),'$VAR'(u)],[max,'$VAR'(l),[min,'$VAR'(u),'$VAR'(x)]]])
(= 
  (clamp $x $l $u) 
  (max $l 
    (min $u $x)))

  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[:,abs,[->,'$VAR'(a),'$VAR'(a)]])
(: abs 
  (-> $a $a))


  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&self',[=,[abs,'$VAR'(x)],[if,[<,'$VAR'(x),0],[*,-1,'$VAR'(x)],'$VAR'(x)]])

    (< $x 0) 
    (* -1 $x) $x))

;;; Define knowledge base for that test
;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;
;;; Rule base for the subtyping relationship ;;
;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;

;;; Notations:
;;;
;;; 1. Variables in upper case, like `$T`, tend to correspond to types.
;;; 2. Variables in lower case, like `$t`, tend to correspond to terms.
;;; 3. In the rule names
;;; 3.1. ST stands for SubTyping,
;;; 3.2. Refl for Reflexive,
;;; 3.3. Trans for transitive,
;;; 3.4. FnTy for Function Type,
;;; 3.5. ImplCoer for Implicit Coercion.

;;; TODO: maybe we should add (: $T Type) as premises

;;; Subtyping is relexive.  WARNING: that one is actually an axiom, not
;;; a rule.
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&rb',[:,'STRefl',[<:,T,T]])
(: STRefl 
  (<: $T $T))


;;; Subtyping is transitive
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&rb',[:,'STTrans',[->,[<:,S,T],[<:,T,U],[<:,S,U]]])
(: STTrans 
  (-> 
    (<: $S $T) 
    (<: $T $U) 
    (<: $S $U)))


;;; Premises
;;; Conclusion
;;; Subtyping of function types is contravariant over inputs and
;;; covariant over outputs.
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&rb',[:,'STFnTy',[->,[<:,T1,S1],[<:,S2,T2],[<:,[->,S1,S2],[->,T1,T2]]]])
(: STFnTy 
  (-> 
    (<: $T1 $S1) 
    (<: $S2 $T2) 
    (<: 
      (-> $S1 $S2) 
      (-> $T1 $T2))))


;;; Premises
;;; Conclusion
;;; Relationship between subtyping and type assuming implicit coercion.
;;; That is if a term `t` is of type `S` a subtype of `T`, then `t` is
;;; of type `T` as well.
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&rb',[:,'STImplCoer',[->,[<:,S,T],[:,T,S],[:,T,T]]])
(: STImplCoer 
  (-> 
    (<: $S $T) 
    (: $T $S) 
    (: $T $T)))


;;; Premises
;;; Conclusion
;;; Relationship between subtyping and type assume explicit coercion.
;;; That is if a term `t` is of type `S` a subtype of `T`, then
;;; `(coerce proof_S<:T t)` is of type `T`, where `proof_S<:T` is a
;;; proof that `S` is a subtype of `T`.
  ; Action: load=asserted_metta_atom('&rb',[:,coerce,[->,[<:,S,T],S,T]])
(: coerce 
  (-> 
    (<: $S $T) $S $T))
